  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_099fd7ec-238c-422d-9a38-483f45a07f58'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText8366406130888803286" style="display:none">For Tristan Hart, everything changes with one crashing wave. <br /><br />He was gone for three days. Sucked out to sea in a tidal wave and spit back ashore at Coney Island with no memory of what happened. Now his dreams are haunted by a terrifying silver mermaid with razor-sharp teeth. <br /><br />His best friend Layla is convinced something is wrong. But how can he explain he can sense emotion like never before? How can he explain he's heir to a kingdom he never knew existed? That he's suddenly a pawn in a battle as ancient as the gods. <br /><br />Something happened to him in those three days. He was claimed by the sea...and now it wants him back.<br /></span>

<div id="review_322710798" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322710798" />
    <a title="Rane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1987431-rane"><img alt="Rane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419878997p2/1987431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/322710798?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rane" href="/user/show/1987431-rane">Rane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=keeper">keeper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=paranormal-pnr-supernatural">paranormal-pnr-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer322710798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5731544884327537974"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376659ra/731624.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> This was fun, fun, FUN! I couldn't get enough of Zoraida Córdova debut novel, from the whole summer feel to *GASP* mermen! Yup! Cordova gave us something totally new with a male lead that is a merman- let the mayhem begin!<br/><br/> Tristan Hart is just your normal <s>horn dog</s> sixteen year old teen. His love for the water just seems to stem from being a great swimmer, and living around Coney Island, New York. Until one day a freak storm appears and Tristan is dragged into the sea, missing for three days wit</span>
  <span id="freeText5731544884327537974" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376659ra/731624.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> This was fun, fun, FUN! I couldn't get enough of Zoraida Córdova debut novel, from the whole summer feel to *GASP* mermen! Yup! Cordova gave us something totally new with a male lead that is a merman- let the mayhem begin!<br><br> Tristan Hart is just your normal <s>horn dog</s> sixteen year old teen. His love for the water just seems to stem from being a great swimmer, and living around Coney Island, New York. Until one day a freak storm appears and Tristan is dragged into the sea, missing for three days without any memory of those days, expect a silver mermaid with shark smile. His feels different since he's been back and everything becomes even more confusing when he grows a tail and his mom use to be a mermaid! Why did it have to be the more girlie fairy tale?<br><br> I loved Tristan cause he was pretty normal teen, he at times could be pretty insensitive, lack tack but on the other side of the coin he had alot of growth and was learning from his past mistakes. His dry wit and sense of humor had me laughing, one was when he grew his tail....<br><br> <blockquote>"I let myself sink up to my shoulders and dangle my arms over the edge. My fins hang out over the brim, curling and uncurling. I wonder where my legs go? I wonder where my dick goes! Holy Crap."</blockquote><br><br> Tristan has alot of important people in his life, through his eyes, you see how special each are in their own way, from his mom and dad, to his friends on the swim team to his "cousins" and his best friend and love Layla, who uses her fists on Tristan when he puts his foot in his mouth. Tristan may been a manhoe, and you can see in high def when his erection and roving eye gets in the way, but with some hard hits along his journey you see the better man he's becoming. <br><br> Zoraida Córdova creates a amazing sea world with bold strokes, and the great idea of a merman being the lead. You see glimpses of the Sea Court and the the other Feyfolk floating about, but with everything on a clock, we're only given a small peek, with a great chance to growth in later books. <br><br> I did have some trouble with some of the actions of the characters, becoming a little irritated with them, but this was quickly overshadowed by their common sense waking up and my enjoyment of the book.<br> Zoradia Cordove hooked me like a prized fish with her amazing novel, that I'm greedily waiting for more from this series and author and more importantly Tristan himself. <br><br> <blockquote>
<br> "but hey, lifeguards are the more naked version of firemen-the girls just love the uniform, in my case, the orange speedo"</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="5731544884327537974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=nook">nook</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198316115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16073902827888204965">Cute book...just <i>not</i> what I was expecting.<br/><br/>From the title and the blurb, I thought this was going to be a much darker/grittier story.<br/>The <b>Vicious</b> Deep. <br/><i>Sucked out to sea...terrifying mermaid with razor sharp teeth...haunted dreams...pawn in a battle as ancient as the gods...</i><br/>Darkish, right?<br/>Except, it's not.<br/><br/>Raise your hand if you've ever seen Disney's Little Mermaid.<br/>Ok, good.<br/>So, this is more like what would happen if Ariel and Eric had a son, and he didn't find out he was half <i>merman</i> until he was ab</span>
  <span id="freeText16073902827888204965" style="display:none">Cute book...just <i>not</i> what I was expecting.<br /><br />From the title and the blurb, I thought this was going to be a much darker/grittier story.<br />The <b>Vicious</b> Deep. <br /><i>Sucked out to sea...terrifying mermaid with razor sharp teeth...haunted dreams...pawn in a battle as ancient as the gods...</i><br />Darkish, right?<br />Except, it's not.<br /><br />Raise your hand if you've ever seen Disney's Little Mermaid.<br />Ok, good.<br />So, this is more like what would happen if Ariel and Eric had a son, and he didn't find out he was half <i>merman</i> until he was about 16 or so. It's pretty light and fluffy, but not necessarily a bad read. In fact, I actually liked it quite a bit.<br />Just don't go into it thinking you're going to get something <b>Vicious</b> or <b>Deep.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16073902827888204965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_619121212" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/619121212" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/619121212?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=fishy-creatures">fishy-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=b-word-heroine">b-word-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer619121212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13643791807658497260">I love mermaids, I really do. Fishy folks just capture my attention, but so far I have been so let down by their depiction in fiction and film. From <i>The Little Mermaid</i> to the <i>Vicious Deep</i> series to the <i>Lullaby</i> series...it seems that the main similarities between fictional merfolk and sirens and other water-dwelling creatures in fiction is not their fins nor their affinity to water, but rather, their absolute stupidity and inability to think like a rational person (not <i>person</i> person, but you get </span>
  <span id="freeText13643791807658497260" style="display:none">I love mermaids, I really do. Fishy folks just capture my attention, but so far I have been so let down by their depiction in fiction and film. From <i>The Little Mermaid</i> to the <i>Vicious Deep</i> series to the <i>Lullaby</i> series...it seems that the main similarities between fictional merfolk and sirens and other water-dwelling creatures in fiction is not their fins nor their affinity to water, but rather, their absolute stupidity and inability to think like a rational person (not <i>person</i> person, but you get the point).<br /><br />The good news is that the mermaids in this book are for the most part, intelligent and tolerable in their lack of annoying TSTL tendencies. The bad part is that the main character's love interest is not, but I will overlook her for the time being, because I am so surprised and pleasantly shocked at the existence of intelligent, functional merfolk in literature. The entire book was enjoyable, hilarious, and fun to read. I found myself laughing out loud more than once. The main characters and supporting cast, with the exception of two, were immensely likeable.<br /><br />The plot focuses on Tristan, he suffers a near-death experience while attempting a rescue during a tsunami-type of situation while working as a lifeguard. In the aftermath, he gets strange dreams of a white-haired, sharp-teethed mermaid, and eventually discovers his true nature as the offspring of a mermaid and a human. Meanwhile, if that's not complicated enough, he is trying to resolve his feelings towards his childhood best friend, Layla...all this while trying to solve a riddle, possibly try to become lord of the sea, and survive death threats by the mysterious mermaid of whom he dreams.<br /><br />I found Tristan to be a likeable character and a good narrator, although his voice does suffer from what I call The Ethan Wates Syndrome. Meaning, he's not entirely convincing as a male character. Tell me, what kind of a male makes these observations?<br /><br /><b>"[The girls] hold paddling boards with Hawaiian flower patterns on them, even though their hair is ironed perfectly straight and their fake eyelashes haven’t been touched by the water."</b><br /><br />...and...<br /><br /><b>"She comes up close, and I can see she doesn’t have any makeup on, except for the pink on her cheeks. No one’s cheeks can be that pink."</b><br /><br />Yeah, things like that are observed by NO REAL STRAIGHT BOY EVER.<br /><br />But those are minor complaints. Besides the odd observation of nail polish or makeup, and the sighing and swooning over his best friend Layla, Tristan is absolutely hilarious as a narrator. More than once, I found myself laughing at the observations he makes and he keeps up a side-splitting commentary, and for the most part, his thoughts are pretty in-line with what a teenaged boy probably thinks upon discovering that he's a merman.<br /><br /><b>"What if he does it wrong and I get stuck like this forever? Can I still have sex with girls or only other mermaids? Where the hell does my dick go?"</b><br /><br />His ragtag groups of friends are your typical group of teenaged male, but they've grown up around each other their entire lives, and are genuinely nice guys at heart; there's nothing to hate about them. His parents are loving, adorable, and absolutely hilarious. You can really see where Tristan become well-adjusted and where he inherited his sense of humor.<br /><br /><b>"'Yeah, yeah. You kids spoiled the wonderful evening your mom and I were having.'<br />'Ugh, disgusting.' I put my fingers in my ears, but I can still hear him laughing. I grab a glass and some OJ.<br />'Oh, come on, son, your merbaby zygote didn’t make itself.'”</b><br /><br />Another character whom I like is Kurt (short for something absolutely unpronounceable), a merman who is acting as Tristan's guide to his new self. He has an unwittingly deadpan sense of humor, and is funny most of the time without meaning to be.<br /><br /><b>“'We do look different. We are glamoured,' Kurt says indignantly. 'It’s a light spell to tone down our natural colors. We are no longer achingly beautiful. Now we’re just exceptionally beautiful.'"</b><br /><br />He knows little about the human world, and as much of a guide he is to Tristan, Tristan is his guide to the human world.<br /><br />Apart from the main cast, even those we originally judge as evil has some redeeming quality, so there aren't many characters I found objectionable.<br /><br />Now, let's get on with the bad. Layla, the most annoying and insipid characters in the book. I cannot imagine the funny, intelligent Tristan would be so stupid to overlook this fact. Tristan has grown up with her his entire childhood, and he is his best friend, even while he dates around (and he is a serial dater). Too late, he realizes that Layla has grown up into a stunning young woman, and while he continues to fall in love with her, from what we see of Layla in the book (and she is a major character), I see nothing about her that is remotely attractive besides her exterior. She is prickly, bitchy (I hate to use this word, but it's accurate), standoffish, and TSTL. Her actions can and did put Tristan and herself in a huge mess, from which they barely escape. <br /><br />Layla is violent (she repeatedly punches Tristan). I don't like violence towards women, and I believe the same standards should exist for guys. It shouldn't be ok for a girl to hit a guy any more than it is for a guy to hit a girl. Tristan tries so hard with her, and most of the time, she just pushes him away.<br /><br /><b>"I keep my eyes on the back of Layla’s head. She doesn’t even turn around to look at me. There is nothing like the silent treatment from the only girl you want to talk to."</b><br /><br />I could itemize the stupid things Layla does in this book to make me dislike her, but there's not enough room in the review. Nevertheless, this is an excellent and funny book, bogged down by very few annoying characters. The cliffhanger is not a terrible one, and I will be continuing with the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13643791807658497260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_293704700" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/293704700" />
    <a title="Experiment BL626" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4582872-experiment-bl626"><img alt="Experiment BL626" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335917426p2/4582872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/293704700?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Experiment BL626" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Experiment BL626" href="/user/show/4582872-experiment-bl626">Experiment BL626</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781402265112" href="/book/show/13630353-the-vicious-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer293704700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11466599545264772255">CAUTION: Long Review.<br/><br/><i>The Vicious Deep</i> begins with Tristan on lifeguard duty at the beach when suddenly a freak wave hits. While everyone runs for their lives, Tristan races to rescue a drowning victim thinking he could make it. Alas, he didn't. Soon, Tristan washes up on shore and taken to the hospital.<br/><br/>People say a near-death experience can be life changing, but with Tristan it reached to a whole new level. <br/><br/>Tristan learned he was lost for three days at sea and was the only survivor of the freak </span>
  <span id="freeText11466599545264772255" style="display:none">CAUTION: Long Review.<br /><br /><i>The Vicious Deep</i> begins with Tristan on lifeguard duty at the beach when suddenly a freak wave hits. While everyone runs for their lives, Tristan races to rescue a drowning victim thinking he could make it. Alas, he didn't. Soon, Tristan washes up on shore and taken to the hospital.<br /><br />People say a near-death experience can be life changing, but with Tristan it reached to a whole new level. <br /><br />Tristan learned he was lost for three days at sea and was the only survivor of the freak wave. Yet he was mostly tired and ready for things to get back to normal. His parents agreed and quickly took him home from the hospital. Barring a few odd occurrences, things seem fine. <br /><br />Till chapter 10.<br /><br />After getting a fishtail for the bottom half of his body, Tristan learned he's a merman, his mother's an ex-mermaid, they're merfolks royalty which made him a Prince.<blockquote>I can forget all that. But of all the creatures in my mom’s fairy-tale books, she had to go and be the girliest? <i>Come on!</i></blockquote><b>The Writing</b><br /><br />TVD had less than 87000 words and was written in present tense, making the action forefront. Imagery was driven by characters' action; character development was driven by dialogue. On occasions, the prose was slightly flowery. <br /><br />Speaking of flowery, the characters cursed using the "mother-flower" euphemism. Fuck, shit, and damn were part of the vernacular but I didn't understand why a variation of fuck would be euphemized. I thought it was silly and stupid. <br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><br />+++ Tristan<br /><br />TVD was told in 1st Pov from Tristan's side. Right from the start, Tristan was not your usual YA protagonist...because he's popular. <br /><br />The YA genre love its loner, its outcast, its "woe is me because I'm a freak and no one understand me" protagonist. Tristan had social skills <i>and</i> enjoyed being around people. In any other YA, he would be the jock love interest our ostracized heroine like because he's nice to her and dislike because his attention to her brings the the mean girls' attention.<br /><br />Tristan is a swimming athlete and a lifeguard, always wearing a Speedo and being flirtatious. His one big flaw was that despite being a girl magnet Tristan treated girls in his relationship quite horribly. Yet it wasn't because he was naturally a jerk. I disliked how Tristan treated Mandy but I pitied him because for all his charm with girls, he couldn't get the one girl that mattered. <br /><br />Tristan was in love with Layla — apparently since childhood — but he didn't how to properly deal with it. <br /><br />+++ Layla<br /><br />Layla is Tristan's love interest and his best friend since childhood. I liked how she refused to be relegated as Tristan's sidekick. She followed Tristan to find out why he has been so secretive and intended to protect him in case he needed help. She stuck with Tristan after learning his secret and sensibly forgave him for not telling her.<br /><br />Far too often in YA the best friend would be mad at our protagonist in beginning, disappear in the middle of the story, and reappear at the end — sometime as a hostage or an antagonist. Layla was not like that; Layla was a strong character in her own rights. <br /><br />+++ Tristan's Parents<br /><br />TVD didn't suffer the <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/ParentalAbandonment" rel="nofollow noopener">Missing Parents Syndrome</a>. Plus, the parents loved each other and their son Tristan. In short, they were genuinely a happy family. It was...<i>unusual</i> because in YA the protagonist's family are always unhappy or dead. Seriously.<br /><br />Mr. Hart was like a geek while Mrs. Hart was like Ariel from Disney's <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Little_Mermaid_%281989_film%29" rel="nofollow noopener">The Little Mermaid</a> because she had red hair and a hobby of collecting junks.<br /><br />+++ Other Characters<br /><br />Tristan's "cousins" Thalia and Kurt were funny. Thalia was carefree and mischievous while Kurt was haughty and magisterial; the two siblings were total opposite in personality. They made great sidekicks to Tristan (technically, they're his royal courtiers).<br /><br />I even liked Gwen the mean mermaid princess. Turned out she was more than I initially thought because I found her meanness warranted. Hell, I would be mean too if I was stuck in her situation. Her family forced her to marry a spoiled merman prince and be happy with the asshole.<br /><br />The other supporting characters such as Marty did not stand out and seem unimportant and unremarkable. The characters from the ship had a muddled introduction.<br /><br /><b>The World Building</b><br /><br />TVD's world was filled with all sorts of supernatural, from vampires to fairies, but the book focused on merfolks. The book used Poseidon from Greek mythology as the basis for its merfolk world. The world building was one of the few unoriginal things about TVD because pretty much every mermaid YA use Poseidon.<br /><br /><b>The Plot</b><br /><br />Tristan's grandfather was nearing his end so he wanted Tristan to replace him as king. However, his grandfather could not directly crown Tristan because the mer-people would revolt. A quest was put forth and Tristan — among other champions — must collect all three dispersed pieces of Poseidon's Trident from three of the five oracles to win the quest and ultimately become the Sea King.<br /><br />The champions must locate the nomadic oracles, figure which one has the Trident piece, and win it from the oracle. Like any other quest to become king, anything goes and survival is part of the goal.<br /><br />I expected the plot to be predictable and largely it was. Yet there were few twists and turns, such as Gwen, that caught me off guard. The book had some slow moments, but for the most part it was quick paced.<br /><br /><b>Things I Didn't Like</b><br /><br />+++ Lack of Parental Involvement<br /><br />I liked the presence of Tristan's parents in the story but I disliked how uninvolved they were in Tristan's quest. They should've fussed about Tristan trying to become the Sea King because 1) he's not an adult 2) he's ignorant of the supernatural world and its danger 3) he wasn't a trained Prince let alone a merman and 4) everyone will try to kill him so they could become king. <br /><br />The only thing I recall the Harts fussing about was Nieve, the distant great-aunt who is crazy and evil and essentially the merfolk's version of the bogeyman. She showed up in Tristan's nightmares and she may be the series' <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_Bad" rel="nofollow noopener">Big Bad</a>.<br /><br />+++ The Awkward Romance<br /><br />Another thing I dislike about TVD was the romance between Tristan and Layla. Their relationship could be summed up in one short sentence: it's complicated. I didn't think it needed to be that way.<br /><br />I thought Tristan spent too much time thinking about Layla and not enough about his quest and his survival.<br /><br />+++ The Ho-hum Hero<br /><br />What mainly stopped me from rating TVD higher was how ho-hum Tristan was as a hero. There was a plot-hole of Tristan knowing how to fight bad mer-guys when he didn't know any martial art or have any fighting experience. All he had was a magical dagger, but it didn't make him a warrior. <br /><br />Beside his magical dagger, his half-merman half-human special status, his look and charm with girl, Tristan didn't exhibit anything special that made him stand out as a hero. He didn't fully grasp the urgency of his quest, the weight of being a king, the secrecy of being a merman, and the danger of it all. Many times I wanted Tristan to stop and think about the depth of the situation.<br /><br /><b>In Conclusion</b><br /><br />I rate TVD for 3 stars for I liked it. TVD may not have been original but it did lack much of the cliché that are prevalent in YA. The plot had some action and comedy, and the protagonist was believable as a teenage male.<br /><br />I recommend TVD for readers looking for something different than your usual YA, readers wanting to jump on the mermaid YA bandwagon, and readers hoping for a light and decent YA read.<br /><br /><b>Memorable Quote</b><blockquote>“Is there a way you can fix that? Make yourselves look different so that you don’t attract so much attention?”<br /><br />“We do look different. We are glamoured,” Kurt says indignantly. “It’s a light spell to tone down our natural colors. We are no longer achingly beautiful. Now we’re just exceptionally beautiful.”</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="11466599545264772255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Gergana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312798-gergana"><img alt="Gergana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439319393p2/5312798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1129473878?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gergana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gergana" href="/user/show/5312798-gergana">Gergana</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/14649078-the-vicious-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312798-gergana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312798-gergana?shelf=find-more">find-more</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1129473878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6187997154884532342">You know those books that have a slow start, but then continue to build up and you can hardly believe the potential and epicness of the story, until you pass the middle and everything is back to the "pretty-good-but-not-the-awesomeness-I-began-to-expect" stage? <br/><br/>Nevertheless, The Vicious Deep is NOTHING like the majority of the YA mermaid books flooding the market - we have a mermen as a protagonist, who is not an angsty, quiet and misunderstood by the world teen, but an outgoing, popular and coc</span>
  <span id="freeText6187997154884532342" style="display:none">You know those books that have a slow start, but then continue to build up and you can hardly believe the potential and epicness of the story, until you pass the middle and everything is back to the "pretty-good-but-not-the-awesomeness-I-began-to-expect" stage? <br /><br />Nevertheless, The Vicious Deep is NOTHING like the majority of the YA mermaid books flooding the market - we have a mermen as a protagonist, who is not an angsty, quiet and misunderstood by the world teen, but an outgoing, popular and cocky kind of guy. The love interest is no damsel in distress, the side characters are just as compelling as the protagonist, if not more, and the villain is...rather boring.<br /><br /><b>So the story begins</b> with a natural disaster, literally. A tsunami that kills many and destroys the beach area! Miraculously, our main hero Tristan - the life guard, who despite the warnings went ahead to try to save the doomed swimmers, survives.<br /><br />I was rather bored at that point and the writing style was not to MY taste. <br /><br /><b>Around Chapter 10 things get interesting though. </b> Tristan turns into a merman in his bathtub and his parents are totally fine and reasonable about it, while their son is having a mental breakdown. Life gets even weirder and funnier when two small fish get into the bathroom through the pipes and transform into humans. They announce that Tristan is requested to attend the Sea King's court and this is where the story picks up.<br /><br />I absolutely loved it when the two mermen guards (Kurt and Thalia) had to go to a human high school and go shopping with Tristan's family. It was hilarious, the dialogue was priceless and the world-building and politics were gradually introduced. Even the side characters and the main love interest were pretty engaging and 3-dimensional.<br /><br />We even get to see the Kingdom of the Sea people and it was stunning, creative and colorful! Like the Mermaid lagoon in Peter Pan only 10 times better, with all kinds of creatures and beautiful landscape! Now, in addition to humor and characters, I was even more impressed with the author's ability to describe imaginary worlds in such vivid detail. <br /><br />Very minor plot spoilers below, but I'll cover them just in case.<br /><br />And then, IT happened -<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[two mermen were at their throats, battling underwater using their tails and fists, trying to cover the opponent's gills and choke him to death! It was intense, it was epic, I was practically on my toes! One of them was left for dead and my expectations just kept going higher. The novel suddenly became serious, the politics - more complex, and to top it all - there are all kinds of magical creatures (fairies, werewolves, vampires, etc. ) in Miss Cordova's world and I was ecstatic! What ELSE will be revealed!<br /><br />Unfortunately, instead of continuing the fast pace, the story slows down, as the characters go back to the human world and ... continue attending high school...through out most of the second half... and deal with relationship problems?!? Whaaaaaaaaa? Seriously!?! <br /><br />True, there are some random shark creatures on legs that attack New Yorkers, true, we get to see Frederick - the super bored and deadly serious vampire (and probably my favorite character next to Kurt), but even the final scene wasn't even close to what I was hoping for.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Conclusion</b><br />Slow start, great humor, creative world, enjoyable characters, amazing middle, disappointing second half with one major exception (a new character that is just too awesome and my favorite, despite his short time in the book), and an alright ending. <br />Am I going to read the sequel - I can't say I'm super excited for it, but there was so much that I loved in this book that it would be a pity not to see what happens next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6187997154884532342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_164847259" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164847259" />
    <a title="Garrett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3772815-garrett"><img alt="Garrett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584253517p2/3772815.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/164847259?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Garrett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Garrett" href="/user/show/3772815-garrett">Garrett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164847259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4303851386235740660">The cover of The Vicious Deep tells you not to let it pull you under. Well, you'll want to do the opposite. Because I'm warning you: this book's just like the whirlpool Tristan encounters in the beginning; it sucks you right in and refuses to let go.<br/>The Vicious Deep is something I never expected to find: a guys' mermaid book. Well, maybe not exactly, more unisex, if anything. There's plenty of kisses and romance for the ladies, but there's also plenty of thrills, action, and fighting for the guy</span>
  <span id="freeText4303851386235740660" style="display:none">The cover of The Vicious Deep tells you not to let it pull you under. Well, you'll want to do the opposite. Because I'm warning you: this book's just like the whirlpool Tristan encounters in the beginning; it sucks you right in and refuses to let go.<br />The Vicious Deep is something I never expected to find: a guys' mermaid book. Well, maybe not exactly, more unisex, if anything. There's plenty of kisses and romance for the ladies, but there's also plenty of thrills, action, and fighting for the guys.<br />TVD can be summed up in one word: FUN. From beginning to end, I laughed and gasped and kept flipping pages. Zoraida's writing style is quick and to-the-point, but also witty and hilarious. There were also many in-jokes that every Little Mermaid fan should pick up on. And if all that hasn't peaked your interest, pick up the book. There are several memorable scenes in the novel that will make you laugh, cry, and sit on the edge of your seat. One of my all-time favorite scenes that had me grinning from ear to ear was the bubble-gum scene. You'll understand.<br />The world of TVD was fully developed too. We not only have traditional mermaids, but all kinds of paranormal creatures, from vampires to werewolves, to fey and shifters. There's a little something from everyone in the book.<br />Probably my favorite thing of the novel was the voice: Tristan. Most mermaid books are from a female perspective, but getting the point of view of a teenage boy as he undergoes his transformation into a merman was funny as it was highly readable. The bathtub scene of Tristan's first transformation was incredibly hilarious.<br />And the other characters! There are so many of them, and each of them so diverse that you won't want to leave their world. From Layla to Gwen, Thalia and Marty, each character felt so real and I didn't want to say goodbye.<br />So if you want good ol' sea monster action, a classic summer love story, a magical trip under the sea, or a seriously creepy villain, dive into The Vicious Deep!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4303851386235740660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_208121339" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/208121339" />
    <a title="Trisha Wolfe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4378990-trisha-wolfe"><img alt="Trisha Wolfe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502379332p2/4378990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/208121339?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trisha Wolfe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trisha Wolfe" href="/user/show/4378990-trisha-wolfe">Trisha Wolfe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer208121339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8219116728475060485">You’ll see me mention voice in a lot of reviews. Some might understand what I mean by it, others might not, but if you want to read something that is a perfect example of “voice”, and how it can transform a character into a three-dimensional, real live person on the page, and suck you so far into a story you feel you’re there, too, then you must read The Vicious Deep. Told from super smokin’ hottie Tristan Hart, TVD grabs you from the first page. With non-stop action, hilarious dialogue, and sin</span>
  <span id="freeText8219116728475060485" style="display:none">You’ll see me mention voice in a lot of reviews. Some might understand what I mean by it, others might not, but if you want to read something that is a perfect example of “voice”, and how it can transform a character into a three-dimensional, real live person on the page, and suck you so far into a story you feel you’re there, too, then you must read The Vicious Deep. Told from super smokin’ hottie Tristan Hart, TVD grabs you from the first page. With non-stop action, hilarious dialogue, and sincere emotions that tug at your heart strings, this story has it all.<br /><br />I cannot stress enough how well Zoraida told this story from a REAL guy’s POV. It was like being inside a guy’s head, no holding back, embarrassing moments and all, and the feelings that guys usually cover with humor or sarcasm are stripped down to their raw truth. It’s just awesome on a whole new level. If that was the only reason to read this book, it would be more than enough, but the story has many layers and an amazing plot, too. Original sea creatures, fun side characters that heighten the adventure, and a deep, memorable romance that made me ache—I’m squirming to get my hands on the next book to find out the next part of Tristan’s story. He is my new book boyfriend and I will fight for him! Oh. Yeah. Powerful and unique, The Vicious Deep gripped me with its edgy voice and authentic, compelling characters. Zoraida Córdova mastered the written word, and created a fearless new world. This is a must read for every YA lover out there. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8219116728475060485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=juvenile-ya">juvenile-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=review-copy-solicited">review-copy-solicited</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=2012-debuts__apocalypsies">2012-debuts__apocalypsies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=mermaids">mermaids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=debut">debut</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167816130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15102843612256717302">The Vicious Depp dammit every time Deep popped up on my radar when <a href='http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-C4kEIsB5M7M/TyLnWoetwOI/AAAAAAAABDc/5vtNxo7yp70/s320/Vicious+Deep.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>this</a> happened, and from that point, I knew I <i>had</i> to read it.  And by the time that <a href='http://www.thebookrat.com/2012/01/friday-face-off-vicious-deep.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>un-happened</a> and a new cover was born, it was so firmly planted in my to-read wishlist that I found myself becoming a member of the Bloggers of the Deep street team. <br/>And for that, I am glad.<br/><br/>The Vicious Deep is a very engaging, somewhat unusual take on mermaids. Riding the crest of the wave of what looks to be a pretty good mermaid craze, TVD forgoes</span>
  <span id="freeText15102843612256717302" style="display:none">The Vicious Depp dammit every time Deep popped up on my radar when <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-C4kEIsB5M7M/TyLnWoetwOI/AAAAAAAABDc/5vtNxo7yp70/s320/Vicious+Deep.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> happened, and from that point, I knew I <i>had</i> to read it.  And by the time that <a href="http://www.thebookrat.com/2012/01/friday-face-off-vicious-deep.html" rel="nofollow noopener">un-happened</a> and a new cover was born, it was so firmly planted in my to-read wishlist that I found myself becoming a member of the Bloggers of the Deep street team. <br />And for that, I am glad.<br /><br />The Vicious Deep is a very engaging, somewhat unusual take on mermaids. Riding the crest of the wave of what looks to be a pretty good mermaid craze, TVD forgoes the expected female heroine and her mysteries of the deep, and follows instead an unsuspecting male lead who finds himself in over his head.  [You see what I did there?  Okay, I'll stop.]  Tristan is likeable: charmingly flawed, self-deprecating yet cocky, typical teenage fuck-up and stunner all in one.  He's one of those guys that, even while you know they're playing you, you can't help but sigh and bat your lashes.  That guy.  And because of that, when he finds himself tossed into this completely unexpected situation where he has to actually put himself out there and <i>try</i> at something that had never even entered his head, it comes together with the way he'd begun to think about his life and <i>trying</i> there, too.  And it just works.<br /><br />His narration is nearly pitch-perfect.  It had a very friend-like feel, like chatting with your besties and the jackasses you hung out with as a teen.  It's a little colloquial and just - authentic feeling, for the most part.  (I'm not now, nor have I ever been, a teenage boy who has just found out he's a mermaidman, so I can't speak to how completely authentic it is...)  It's just very funny and cheeky and teenagery in a not-so-angsty way (and AMEN for that).  The voice is just great.  It played well off of the other characters, too, which I think was one of the strong points of the novel.   I really enjoyed the characters and their interactions, and the fact that there is some gray area within them. Tristan is not always a shining hero, (for all that he is shin<i>y</i>), and some of the more dubious, possibly villainous characters turn out to be pretty okay (I love Gwen! #GwenFTW!)<br /><br />The characters draw you in, but I think the story is enjoyable in other respects, too.  At its heart, it's a good, rollicking adventure story with a bit of heart and charm at the core; a thread of romancifulness and a dash of badassery.  It's something that will appeal to both genders, I think, and could easily transition to the big screen.  It's a bit of a more grown-up Percy Jackson - a little less wholesome and cutesy, and a little more...vicious, with a mythology all its own and solid, enjoyable world-building.<br /><br />For awhile, I was held back a little bit by the <i>necessity </i>of the story. There were questions, the foremost being, Why does Tristan need to become Sea King?  Why should he even care, and how is he in ANY way qualified?  (I come from a Kingless place, you'll remember.  We stopped believing in de jure divine some time ago...)  But where so many YA books wouldn't have addressed it, Córdova DID, and that won me over big time.  Someone <u>flat-out asks</u> Tristan why he gives a flying fuck (? swimming shi-..nevermind), and he actually does stop to consider the choice he could make (to ignore it, to let someone else deal with it, to wonder what his place is in all of it), and then makes a decision based on heart and instinct.  I respected that; not only that he is <i>choosing</i> to go down this path, but that he (and Córdova)  recognizes that there <i>would </i>be questions and other paths, and that <i>thought</i> does need to go into the decision.  This got points, friends.  Points* in the meaningless scoreboard that is my head.<br /><br />I have to say, there will be those that are put off by the fact that there's a lot of build up for not all that much accomplished in the end.  I don't want this to sound like nothing happens; I just mean there's a lot still in the air at the end, and the story has really just begun. But it's a trilogy, so that's something any regular reader should see coming a mile (fathom?) away. Also, I think it made for good world-building, and things would have been much less believable and weighty if everything had been solved in this book and tied up with a pretty little bow.  Things can happen a little quicker now in the rest of the series, and still have a good foundation as a result of the time spent building the story in this first book.  So I didn't have an issue with where things stand at the end, but it just bears mentioning, I think.<br /><br />So yeah.  The Vicious Deep.  Fun for a girl and a boy.  (Though I still wish it had <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-C4kEIsB5M7M/TyLnWoetwOI/AAAAAAAABDc/5vtNxo7yp70/s320/Vicious+Deep.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> cover.  Though I know it would pretty much mean =/= fun for boys, cause they'd never pick it up...)<br /><br />*1000 points redeemable for a slinky or sticky slap-hand.  Winners choice!<br /><br />Don't forget to check out my <a href="http://www.thebookrat.com/2012/04/mermaid-anatomy-guest-vlog-from-zoraida.html" rel="nofollow noopener">guest vlog on merbits</a> from Zoraida, and <a href="http://www.thebookrat.com/2012/04/giveaway-vicious-deep.html" rel="nofollow noopener">enter to win</a> a copy of The Vicious Deep! (ends May 5th)<br /><br />[Oh, and I guess I should note, I read an ARC of this, so things may be different in the final version!]</span>
  <a data-text-id="15102843612256717302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_300996450" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300996450" />
    <a title="Leigh Collazo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4141951-leigh-collazo"><img alt="Leigh Collazo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589123295p2/4141951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300996450?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leigh Collazo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leigh Collazo" href="/user/show/4141951-leigh-collazo">Leigh Collazo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4141951-leigh-collazo?shelf=pub-date-2012">pub-date-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4141951-leigh-collazo?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300996450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11896704656430215965"><br/>More reviews at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://readerpants.blogspot.com'>http://readerpants.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/><b>REVIEW:</b> On the surface, <i>Vicious Deep</i> has all the ingredients that I love to see in a YA novel: a male protagonist, a seemingly unattainable romance, mermaids and an assortment of mythological sea creatures, snarky humor, a quest to find an oracle... but I can't say I loved this book. For one thing, it took me THREE WEEKS to finish reading it. I kept putting it down, falling asleep after three pages, reading other books "in between." Why did that hap</span>
  <span id="freeText11896704656430215965" style="display:none"><br />More reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://readerpants.blogspot.com">http://readerpants.blogspot.com</a><br /><br /><b>REVIEW:</b> On the surface, <i>Vicious Deep</i> has all the ingredients that I love to see in a YA novel: a male protagonist, a seemingly unattainable romance, mermaids and an assortment of mythological sea creatures, snarky humor, a quest to find an oracle... but I can't say I loved this book. For one thing, it took me THREE WEEKS to finish reading it. I kept putting it down, falling asleep after three pages, reading other books "in between." Why did that happen? Why was I so disconnected with the characters and the story? I absolutely adore mermaid literature, and male protagonist/ unwitting merman Tristan is likeable and funny. While Layla kind of irritates me with her never-ending spunk, the characters are mostly pretty likeable and clearly-drawn. <br /><br />So why didn't I like the book? One word: pacing. Very little actually happens in the novel's 380 pages. There is a lot of talk about what's going to happen, what's happening to Tristan's body, what's going down in the mermaid community. I would have loved to see more connection between Tristan and Layla. On one hand, Tristan loves Layla more than just about anything, but he also checks out the female mermaids quite frequently. He's an insatiable flirt who knows girls find him attractive, and he sometimes uses that to get girls to do what he wants them to do. That may be realistic, but it doesn't make me really root for Tristan to end up with Layla. <br /><br />I wish there were fewer instances of gratuitous language and references to Tristan's "junk." Profanity does not bother me (my husband likes to call me "Captain" because I "cuss like a sailor"), but I think the profanity usage in <i>Vicious Deep</i> is unnecessary. Even though I didn't love the pacing, I would have put <i>Vicious Deep</i> in my middle school library if it weren't for the frequency of the F-word and references to Tristan's "junk." I do have many books in my library that include profanity and sexual references, but I hate it when mature content seems thrown in just for the heck of it. <br /><br />All that said, I have no doubt <i>Vicious Deep</i> will be a successful book. The cover is gorgeous, there's a male protagonist, and mermaids are hot right now. All the reviews I've seen praise it highly, and the Goodreads rating is well over 4-stars. It's not bad or terrible; it just didn't do much for me. <br /><br /><b>THE BOTTOM LINE:</b> While for me, <i>Vicious Deep</i> has serious pacing issues and too much unnecessary profanity, I believe it will be a successful novel that will appeal to many teens. For middle school librarians concerned about mature content, check out <i>Lies Beneath<a href="http://readerpants.blogspot.com/search/label/Lies%20Beneath" rel="nofollow noopener"></a></i>.<br /><br /><b>STATUS IN MY LIBRARY:</b> I can't get this one for middle school; see content advisory below. Highly recommended for high school libraries.<br /><br /><b>READALIKES:</b> <i>Lies Beneath</i> (Anne Greenwood Brown)<br /><br /><b>RATING BREAKDOWN:</b> <br /> 
  <br />
   Overall: 3/5 
  <br />
   Creativity: 4/5 
  <br />
   Characters: 4/5 
  <br />
   Engrossing: 1/5  
  <br />
   Writing: 2/5 
  <br />
   Appeal to teens: 5/5 
  <br />
   Appropriate length to tell the story: 2/5 
  <br />
 <br /><br /><b>CONTENT: </b> <br /> 
  <br />
   Language: medium-high; includes multiple instances of sh** and fu** 
  <br />
    Sexuality: medium; multiple references to Tristan's manhood (Such as where does "it" go when he transforms, feeling "heat" in his pants); a few mild kissing scenes  
  <br />
   Violence: mild-medium; some sea creature deaths (somewhat bloody/gory but also kind of funny); two human deaths (gory but not too descriptive) 
  <br />
    Drugs/Alcohol: mild; a couple of scenes where teens drink (one unknowingly gets drunk). Neither scene is a big deal unless you are completely opposed to teen drinking in YA books.

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_367882801" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/367882801" />
    <a title="Heidi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5463965-heidi"><img alt="Heidi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326677199p2/5463965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/367882801?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi" href="/user/show/5463965-heidi">Heidi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/14649078-the-vicious-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer367882801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5102973755763831233"><br/>Three Stars: A fun book with mermen and more! <br/><br/>Tristan is enjoying another lifeguard shift at the Coney Island Beach.  He watches the sun kissed girls in skimpy bikinis and sunglasses parading up and down the beach, a catwalk for the lifeguards.  His eyes dart over them, but in reality he only has eyes for one girl, Layla, who just happens to be his best friend and has no idea of his feelings.  The lazy afternoon is interrupted without warning when screams pierce the air.  A giant wave is headed </span>
  <span id="freeText5102973755763831233" style="display:none"><br />Three Stars: A fun book with mermen and more! <br /><br />Tristan is enjoying another lifeguard shift at the Coney Island Beach.  He watches the sun kissed girls in skimpy bikinis and sunglasses parading up and down the beach, a catwalk for the lifeguards.  His eyes dart over them, but in reality he only has eyes for one girl, Layla, who just happens to be his best friend and has no idea of his feelings.  The lazy afternoon is interrupted without warning when screams pierce the air.  A giant wave is headed toward shore and in its wake are hundreds of screaming beach goers.  Tristan looks out at the dark water and sees a pair of arms struggling in the water.  Without thinking, he runs toward the water despite Layla's frantic screams.  He plunges in, only to find the current is too strong and the victim yards away.  The behemoth wave crashes over him, and he fades into blackness.  Three days later, he awakens on the beach to the joyful squeals of Layla.  His return is miraculous! Yet, where was he for those three days?  Why does he remember nothing except a woman with white hair and vicious teeth, and a shark?  It seems that Tristan's mother has been keeping some secrets from him.  Secrets that will change everything, including his future and those secrets lie in the Vicious Deep....<br /><br />What I Liked:<br />*I appreciated reading this one from a male's perspective.  There are not enough male point of view books in the YA genre, so I am always pleased to find a male narrator.  Tristan is funny and courageous as well as a typical male, in that he doesn't always make the best decisions when it comes to dating and he is overly concerned with his male parts.  I also enjoyed that he is a merman, which again is not something you find in the sea of books.<br />*I liked that this book presents a complex story line.  It has numerous storylines: Tristan discovering his true identity and battling for his chance as a ruler, Tristan's unrequited feelings for his best friend Layla, the challenging quest in order to become the sea king, avoiding the dangerous sea witch and Merrows....these storylines blend into an action filled story line.<br />*I enjoyed the romance in this one.  It consists of two lifelong best friends who obviously have feelings for each other, but neither party has expressed or acknowledged their feelings toward the other.  Thus, you get a romance with smoldering tension that leaves the reader anxiously waiting for that pivotal moment that changes everything and for the sparks to start flying.  No insta love or love triangles in this one!<br />*This book has may memorable characters that are just as fun and entertaining as the protagonists.  I especially enjoyed Marty, the mysterious boy who is not completely human.  This book is full of great memorable characters.  The Sea King is also fascinating. <br />*I loved how the incorporated the sense of smell into the book.  She cleverly uses it to describe feelings, I liked the additional sensory experience in her writing. It was certainly unique and refreshing. <br /><br />And The Not So Much:<br />*My biggest complaint for this book might seem petty to some of you, but to me it was like nails across the chalkboard every time I encountered this flaw.  What was the offender?  This book on countless occasions uses the phrases "I go" or "he goes" or "she goes" instead of saying I said or he/she said.  It is not grammatically correct to use this slang and I was absolutely shocked to find it in this book. I cannot believe a professional editor let that slide.  I also found the phrase "and he/she was all" annoying along with the constant use of "bro".<br />*I was a bit disappointed that Tristan's  mother and her history did not play a bigger role.  This seemed like such an important piece of the story.  How does a mermaid fall for a land dweller and what are all the repercussions?   Too much of this was left out and glossed over.  I truly wanted to know all these details. <br />*This book has a complex story line with many conflicts and plots playing out, the problem is that almost none of them are resolved by the end of the book and the reader is left with another big fat, dreadful cliffhanger.  A big let down! <br /><br />The Vicious Deep is an entertaining and action packed read that follows a young man as he discovers the shocking truth of his heritage and the subsequent consequences of being a Merman who is in love with his best friend.  If you are looking for a mermaid book that is a bit different give this a try.  Tristan is a likeable hero who will make you laugh with his antics.  Look for the follow up: The Savage Blue, January 2013.<br /><br />Favorite Quotations:<br /><br />"Her lips are warm, like leaning your face up at the sky and wishing the sun would kiss you, and it does.  It really does."<br /><br />"Sometimes I'd tell her she and Dad should've tried for a daughter, and then realized I was telling my parents to keep having sex."<br /><br />"The smell of disappointment that's coming from her---crushed flowers and dew and the fog before it rains."<br /><br />"I don't need a sixth sense to describe the way she smells today, like sunshine in this terribly cloudy day."<br /><br />"My heart feels like a Hacky Sack in use when she says Layla's name."<br /><br />"I can sense her near me---lavender and salt and crushed flowers, sticky between her fingertips.  She loves me not."<br /><br />"The ground beneath us glitters.  The river ends in a waterfall that falls like silk against the boulders."<br /><br />"I can smell Layla's wonder, her own blend of blooming flowers."<br /><br />"When you grow up without grandparents, it's like you're missing a link to a past you didn't even care you had until you have to sort through it to understand who you are."<br /><br />"I'm half human.  Not half stupid." Most of the time."<br /><br />"I don't like my girls with a side of crazy, thank you."<br /><br />This review and quotes are from an ARC copy I received in exchange for an honest review.  I received no compensation and all opinions expressed are my own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5102973755763831233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1637828143294637609">3.5 Stars Rounding down.<br/><br/>This book started out great, lots of humor, dirty jokes, and it was written in a guy's POV which just made it that much more funny. I am still not sure what to make of Tristan, sometimes I liked him others not so much, but by the end of the book I still feel undecided...There is just something about him that is missing. It almost feels like when you are in shock, you can see everything that's going on but you don't truly feel anything, and that's what it felt like at some</span>
  <span id="freeText1637828143294637609" style="display:none">3.5 Stars Rounding down.<br /><br />This book started out great, lots of humor, dirty jokes, and it was written in a guy's POV which just made it that much more funny. I am still not sure what to make of Tristan, sometimes I liked him others not so much, but by the end of the book I still feel undecided...There is just something about him that is missing. It almost feels like when you are in shock, you can see everything that's going on but you don't truly feel anything, and that's what it felt like at some points. <br /><br />Part 2 and 3 is when you really get into the 'plot' which for now is really just a quest to get the trident so he can become the next Sea King. There was plenty of action and I really enjoyed those scenes, but by part 3 I was skimming every few paragraphs. It just wasn't grabbing my attention as much like in the first part except when you got to the fight scenes. <br /><br />Since this is the first book in a series, it was left with quite a bit of things left hanging loose. The romance was left up in the air, don't really know what is going on there, and with the plot, I mean I get what they are trying to do and the threat with the sea witch but I am still waiting for the other shoe to drop. <br /><br />I still really enjoyed this book since one it was written in a boy's POV and they put a new conflict to the merman story line beside the whole picking where they are going to live. He will eventually have to decide but the politics of their world takes a much more important role. Will be reading the next in the series to follow Tristan's quest.</span>

  <span id="freeText10173047382672337710" style="display:none">It begans strong, and it attracted me with all the mistery of what is going on. <span id="freeTextContainer18197528971319986572">Loved this book! So action-packed- had me sitting on the edge of my seat for the whole 3 hours I read it!! <br/>Praise to the author for writing a new amazing series! Hope you don't take too long writing the sequel I don't think I can wait! </span>

          </span>

    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4277731-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384212540p2/4277731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/331841253?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/4277731-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=mermaids">mermaids</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331841253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1832830099030688139"><br/><a href='http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2012/10/the-vicious-deep-by-zoraida-cordova.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Find this review at Scott Reads It</a><br/><a href='http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2012/10/interview-with-zoraida-cordova-author.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Check out my interview with Zoraida Córdova!</a><br/>“He was claimed by the sea...and now it wants him back.”<br/> Thank you to Goodreads which helped me find the Vicious Deep! I found it on a listopia for YA Mermaid books and I was so excited to find a book from the point of view of a merman. I also met Zoraida Cordóva at an annual book festival and she was very kind and friendly! Also my Goodreads friend Dr. Bob recommended it to me which made me want to read it even more!<br/> </span>
  <span id="freeText1832830099030688139" style="display:none"><br><a href="http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2012/10/the-vicious-deep-by-zoraida-cordova.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Find this review at Scott Reads It</a><br><a href="http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2012/10/interview-with-zoraida-cordova-author.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Check out my interview with Zoraida Córdova!</a><br>“He was claimed by the sea...and now it wants him back.”<br> Thank you to Goodreads which helped me find the Vicious Deep! I found it on a listopia for YA Mermaid books and I was so excited to find a book from the point of view of a merman. I also met Zoraida Cordóva at an annual book festival and she was very kind and friendly! Also my Goodreads friend Dr. Bob recommended it to me which made me want to read it even more!<br> <br> I really loved the Vicious Deep! It was told from the point of view of Tristan Hart who at first seemed like a bit of a jerk but he really proved himself to be a true hero and just an awesome character. Tristan was a realistic teenage boy that I felt like I could really relate to! Tristan was out at sea missing for 3 days and he keeps having visions of a mermaid with sharp teeth. Tristan can tell no one not even his best friend Layla about what he is going through. Tristan must travel to the Sea Court to meet the merfolk and he is truly in for the adventure of his life!<br> <br> The Vicious Deep was such a fast and fun read! I loved how funny Tristan was and I couldn't stop laughing while I was reading. Seriously my family members probably thought I had something wrong with me because I was laughing so much! The action scenes were so exciting to read and I couldn't stop reading! This was my reaction to my family members while reading! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/492383.gif" width="300" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Nothing else mattered while I read The Vicious Deep because I was too busy in the world of merfolk. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380378097ra/733521.gif" width="300" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Seriously next time I go swimming I really hope I grow a merman tail. A guy can hope right? Okay now I'm just getting way off topic. The Vicious Deep was seriously the epitome of awesomeness. I am not exaggerating at all. The Vicious Deep had awesome sea monster battles, mermen, and lots of humor.What else could you ask for?? I really loved how it was told from a male pov and how fast paced it was. It was amazing how realistic the POV was in this book and I seriously wish it was longer :) I was not bored at all while reading Córdova's debut and I really really really x1000 want an ARC of the Savage Blue! Pretty Please Sourcebooks, how could you resist Agnes? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/432862.gif" width="300" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> If you haven't read the Vicious Deep yet and you are still questioning whether you should read it. You must read it because I know you'll just love it. Why are you still reading this? Go read the Vicious Deep already and you won't be disappointed! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1832830099030688139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Afterall, Tristan is nothing like Ariel or Eric xD<br><br>Well i had fun reading this book. Like i said, it was not something i got used to (too much vampire and werewolves, demons and angels) and i needed something refreshing. Read it, you won't regret :) <br></span>

<div id="review_272899564" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272899564" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5034014-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374602338p2/5034014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272899564?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5034014-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272899564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2929028554059054348">Meet Tristan - man-slut, popular, life-guard, ultra-pretty-boy, average intelligence.<br/><br/>Tristan's life, up until the beginning of the book, is pretty straightforward. In fact his life is easy.<br/><br/>But all that's about to change because...HE'S A MERMAID! Wait, they prefer the term Merman. Cause that's 10,000 times more manly.<br/><br/>So, Merman Tristan discovers that he is, in fact, related to the Sea King, the ruler of all merpeople, his mother being a princess. Turns out, his grandfather is nearing the end of h</span>
  <span id="freeText2929028554059054348" style="display:none">Meet Tristan - man-slut, popular, life-guard, ultra-pretty-boy, average intelligence.<br /><br />Tristan's life, up until the beginning of the book, is pretty straightforward. In fact his life is easy.<br /><br />But all that's about to change because...HE'S A MERMAID! Wait, they prefer the term Merman. Cause that's 10,000 times more manly.<br /><br />So, Merman Tristan discovers that he is, in fact, related to the Sea King, the ruler of all merpeople, his mother being a princess. Turns out, his grandfather is nearing the end of his reign, and needs a heir, and <i>soon.</i> Naturally, Tristan is a viable candidate.<br /><br />I liked this, for the most part. The main issue I had is that I never connected with anyone in the story. Tristan in particular. He, as we're constantly reminded, is a popular guy/man-slut (since he constantly reminds us that he is the Panty Charmer), but we never see that side of him. Technically, he's in love with one girl in particular during the story, which might be why we never see his previous-to-book-beginning version (it's suppressed?). Basically, Tristan doesn't match the image his background description paints, or his stereotype. He also has no defining characteristics that set him apart. I didn't really root for him, either.<br /><br />Also, Tristan adapts far too quickly to being a Mermaid, the entire supernatural world, actually. He gets angry for like a second (with his parents) then it's <i>♫ Mermaids ain't shit and they ain't sayin' nothin', a hundred vampires can't tell me nothin' ♫</i>.<br /><br />The plot pacing is also off a wee bit. I didn't notice it enough to go into it, so I won't. The plot itself could use some better direction, it didn't develop very naturally, or interestingly to maintain reader interest. At least mine, until the 2/3 of the way in when it picked up.<br /><br />That's really it. Mostly worth a read, if there's nothing more pressing on your plate. Nothing really new, no genre-busting stuff. Probably reading the sequel.<br /><br />P.S.: All Mermaids are super-beautiful, scantily clad vixens. Just tossing that out there. Ariel was one of the uglier ones, she's generally frowned upon by the mermaid community.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2929028554059054348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
